### Post by gymophett on 2009-08-31
> * Stay within the board rules, no matter how hot you may believe the wallpaper/screen shot to be.
* If you are going to quote, there isn't a need to quote an img-embeded picture - Just don't do it. Please just reference the post by page number/page link/etc.
* Off Topic Posts will be edited or removed.
* The desktops thread is not to be used as a means to post explicit or suggestive, and provocative images (they must be safe for your kids and/or boss to see). Please help to keep the thread relevant and safe to browse for everyone.
* The moderators of this forum reserve the right to edit or remove your posts as necessary so they may comply with our Community Rule set.
* Please use reduced-size thumbnails, where possible, out of respect for people running on lower bandwidth or screen resolutions.
* To avoid having users having to ask you for them. we request that you format your posts in the following order:

Themes: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

Wallpaper: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

Icons: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

Programs: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).
Important Note: Any image posted that is over 800 x 600 will be removed! Use a thumbnail or use a text link to your image. If your image is removed, this is why.

Mine for today. :) Wall-E rocks.

### Post by sideaway on 2009-09-02
> **vrkalak said:**
> LinuxMint-7 (Gnome) or Xubuntu (Xfce)

Damn ... how do I make my thumbnail into a thumbnail?  :(

[URL="http://farm4.static.flickr.com/3452/3876504610_4df90ca052_t_d.jpg"][img]http://farm4.static.flickr.com/3452/3876504610_4df90ca052_t.jpg[/img]
[/URL]
```


[*URL="http://farm4.static.flickr.com/3452/3876504610_4df90ca052_t_d.jpg"][*img]http://farm4.static.flickr.com/3452/3876504610_4df90ca052_t.jpg[/img]
[/URL]
```

replace ```
[*img]http://farm4.static.flickr.com/3452/3876504610_4df90ca052_t.jpg[/img]
```
with a URL to a bigger version of your desktop.

alternatively. upload a big version to [www.hdimage.org](www.hdimage.org) or [www.imageshack.us](www.imageshack.us) and it will generate a thumbnail for you.

### Post by uberdonkey5 on 2009-09-02
Well, this is pretty simple I use pilgrim theme, but made the colours of the boxes slightly minty inside.

Wallpaper - simple and easy to see icons on top (yes, I like to use my desktop for folders also)

icons are nuoveXT.2.2

I seem to have stuck with this for a while now, so satisfies my tastes and is practical.

I don't really like the docks, instead I have a panel on the left and right (since I use widescreen, makes more sense than having panels on top or bottom).

You may notice I have the frequency of each of my two CPUs (just for reassurance that they are both working nicely, also allows me to save energy by limiting max frequency)

Also have System Monitor aplet on the left (blue=processors, red= network). Network monitor is really useful as sometimes my modem seems to slow down, so I can see if I am actually receiving data.

Applet above shutdown icon (on right) actually allows timed shutdown after [user input] number of minutes... which I love cos I often listen to radio at night and get my computer to shutdown when program finishes.

### Post by nitelite on 2009-09-02
> **kamitsukai said:**
> How did you get the partial transparency in Dolphin? (I'm new to kde...)


It's the widget theme Bespin that now supports ARGB transperency. the transperency

shows up in all apps/programs opened. see below link to enable it.

[http://www.kde-look.org/content/show.php/Bespin?content=63928](http://www.kde-look.org/content/show.php/Bespin?content=63928)

I think soon we will see it in the Bespin hacks settings for easy enable.

### Post by Islington on 2009-09-02

Got it right this time. The correct way to compile this:

```

svn co blah blah blah
cd cloudcity
mkdir build
cd ../
./configure
Y
Y
c
g
make
sudo make install

```

### Post by Alfons81 on 2009-09-03
This is my desktop on Ubuntu 9.04 amd64:

Window manager > Openbox

GTK2 theme > [Dark_star ]("http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Dark_Star?content=110767")

Openbox theme > [Black-grass ]("http://cutebuntu.moonthology.org/2009/04/18/black-grass/")

Panel > Tint2 ( I've to fix seconds, on clock time ) 

System monitor > Conky (my [conkyrc]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=281865&highlight=conkyrc&page=896") > 

Tray ( actually not on the screenshoots ) > Trayer

Dock > Wbar 

Icons on Wbar > mixure between [Minty ]("http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Minty+Leaf+Iconset+by+mickyz?content=107461"), [Icomity]("http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/iComity?content=94079"), [Cryo64-mixed]("http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Cryo64-Mixed?content=107287") and [Mashup]("http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Mashup?content=86452")

File manager > Pcmanfm

Icons on file manager > [Oxygen-Refit 2 - Green Version]("http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Oxygen-Refit+2+-+Green+Version?content=84683")

Wallpaper > A Perfect Morning at Glacier National Park ([flickr]("http://www.flickr.com/photos/stuckincustoms/2746960560/")) is a HDR photo made by [Trey Ratcliff]("http://www.stuckincustoms.com/") who is doing an amazing job.

Audioplayer > Audacious 

Audacious skin > [Bunjee ]("http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/bunjee+++++%26+VUmeter?content=71828")

Fonts > Android

Hope you like it.

### Post by kzlazy on 2009-09-04
> **Stan_1936 said:**
> What theme is that?  And what mouse cursor?

The theme is compiz murrina (see gnome-look.org) with a change of the color scheme (it originally has red scrollbars and looks darker thus causing a lousy effect on openoffice toolbars, if I remember well).

The cursor is in the repos (see oxygen-cursor-theme and the package with the extra colors).

As for the wallpaper (asked by another forum member) I cannot remember anymore where I found it. I think it was in photo forum.

### Post by sertse on 2009-09-05
> **DownTown22 said:**
> Ummmm......no.

> **Tipped OuT said:**
> Yeah, I'm not seeing it either...:???: Care to explain sertse?

Look closely at my Xfce settings control panel. "Qt 4 Settings" and "Desktop Session Settings" (Lxde session editor), aren't exactly....typical things you see there right? 

There's a config option in the .desktop files that decides whether something is shown in the xfce control panel. It done by adding "X-XFCE" and "DesktopSettings" in the categories section of the .desktop file. I could place Firefox there if I want to by setting the option hahaha :D. 

I thought I'll share it to help those of us who like to make our desktops feel a little bit more integrated. :)

> **pelle.k said:**
> Here you go (attachment). It's a quick packaging effort i made to test pragha out on _jaunty_. It may, or may not, work very well.

Thanks for the effort. :) It'll might sound bad though, that I compiled it since my post this morning and now... :S

### Post by N00b-un-2 on 2009-09-06
it's pretty 'mac' ish.  I use the global menu and a dock at the bottom because I find the Mac OS to flow better.  I use gimp quite a bit, so having the menu at the top is just a much better way to do business.
I'm using AWN with a custom theme.  I tried out Docky for a bit, but it doesn't have a lot of functionality implemented yet --and yes, I have built Do from the latest release.  It's a good dock, but it needs some work.  Not being able to theme it is a deal breaker for me though.
My icon set is Hydroxygen Brown (my favorite set for Linux).  I'm using a modified "Art Of Cappuccino" GTK theme and Gilouche for my window border decoration.
The wallpaper is a spoof on one of my favorite wallpapers for OSX that I created on Gimp, but done in a distinctively Ubuntu flavor.  If you would like a copy of my wallpaper, let me know

### Post by ad_267 on 2009-09-06
> **Rasi said:**
> Because its soo hard to bind a key yourself? 
No, because I shouldn't have to. [https://bugs.kde.org/show_bug.cgi?id=166608](https://bugs.kde.org/show_bug.cgi?id=166608)

> KDE mounts all my usb drives automatically and i never had to configure anything for this to happen. I guess if it isnt working its either ubuntus fault or yours :)

KDE mounts them if I open them with Dolphin or another KDE application. For various reasons sometimes I want to mount them without having to open dolphin. Gnome, Windows and Mac all do this but not KDE. [https://bugs.kde.org/show_bug.cgi?id=164053](https://bugs.kde.org/show_bug.cgi?id=164053)

Other than that I like KDE and use it as well as Gnome, it was just a bit of a dig at the person saying KDE was amazing.

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2009-09-10
> **el mariachi said:**
> guys I'm trying to create a theme but I have some problems with colors (I'm daltonic/color blind) is there any software that outputs the name of a color based on it's hex code?

How would that be any more helpful than reading the hex codes, themselves?

FTR, the alphabet used is 0-9, then A-F. Hex codes are separated into RGB values, so the first two digits are your red value, third and fourth are green, and the last two are blue.

### Post by Amtal on 2009-09-12
> **dbbolton said:**
> Could you pastebin the working script? The code in the codebox seems corrupt:

Sorry about that, didn't realize.  I'll put the code in here and keep a mirror up on my DropBox site.

[http://dl.getdropbox.com/u/116194/Scripts/colortheme.sh](http://dl.getdropbox.com/u/116194/Scripts/colortheme.sh)


```
#!/bin/bash
# Original: http://frexx.de/xterm-256-notes/
#           http://frexx.de/xterm-256-notes/data/colortable16.sh
# Modified by Aaron Griffin


FGNAMES=(' black' '   red' ' green' 'yellow' '  blue' 'magnta' '  cyan' ' white')
BGNAMES=('BLK' 'RED' 'GRN' 'YEL' 'BLU' 'MAG' 'CYN' 'WHT')
for b in $(seq 0 7); do
    bg=$(($b+40))

    echo -en "\033[0m ${BGNAMES[$b]} :: "
        for f in $(seq 0 7); do
                echo -en "\033[${bg}m\033[$(($f+30))m ${FGNAMES[$f]} "
    done

    echo -en "\033[0m\n\033[0m     :: "
        for f in $(seq 0 7); do
                echo -en "\033[${bg}m\033[1;$(($f+30))m ${FGNAMES[$f]} "
    done
        echo -e "\033[0m"

    if [ "$b" -lt 7 ]; then
        echo "     -------------------------------------------------------------------"
    fi
done

echo
echo

```

### Post by dbbolton on 2009-09-12
> **Amtal said:**
> Sorry about that, didn't realize.  I'll put the code in here and keep a mirror up on my DropBox site.

[http://dl.getdropbox.com/u/116194/Scripts/colortheme.sh](http://dl.getdropbox.com/u/116194/Scripts/colortheme.sh)


```
#!/bin/bash
# Original: http://frexx.de/xterm-256-notes/
#           http://frexx.de/xterm-256-notes/data/colortable16.sh
# Modified by Aaron Griffin


FGNAMES=(' black' '   red' ' green' 'yellow' '  blue' 'magnta' '  cyan' ' white')
BGNAMES=('BLK' 'RED' 'GRN' 'YEL' 'BLU' 'MAG' 'CYN' 'WHT')
for b in $(seq 0 7); do
    bg=$(($b+40))

    echo -en "\033[0m ${BGNAMES[$b]} :: "
        for f in $(seq 0 7); do
                echo -en "\033[${bg}m\033[$(($f+30))m ${FGNAMES[$f]} "
    done

    echo -en "\033[0m\n\033[0m     :: "
        for f in $(seq 0 7); do
                echo -en "\033[${bg}m\033[1;$(($f+30))m ${FGNAMES[$f]} "
    done
        echo -e "\033[0m"

    if [ "$b" -lt 7 ]; then
        echo "     -------------------------------------------------------------------"
    fi
done

echo
echo

```
Good news everyone! It works perfectly. Thanks.

### Post by Amtal on 2009-09-12
> **purgatori said:**
> Thanks :) Unfortunately, when I attempt to execute the script, it errors out with:

```
colortheme.sh: 7: Syntax error: "(" unexpected
```

EDIT: On second thought, it is a bash shell script.  Are you trying to run it in a different shell and do you have bash installed?  You could try chaning "#!/bin/bash" to "#!/bin/sh", though I don't know if the script uses any of the bash-specific features talked about below.

From [Wikipedia]("http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bash#Portability"):> Shell scripts written with Bash-specific features (bashisms) will not function on a system using the Bourne shell or one of its replacements, unless Bash is installed as a secondary shell and the script begins with #!/bin/bash (known as the "shebang line"). This problem became particularly important when Ubuntu began to ship the Debian Almquist shell (dash) as the default scripting shell in October 2006, causing a wide variety of scripts to fail.

### Post by londonali1010 on 2009-09-14
> **Dharmachakra said:**
> Now, I'm wondering if someone can help with something I'm trying to fix. Check out the screenshot below...

[[IMG]http://img32.imageshack.us/img32/4157/screenshot1lr.th.png[/IMG]](http://img32.imageshack.us/i/screenshot1lr.png/)

See how the shadow from the panel overlaps the top of the browser window? I'm wondering if there's any Compiz options to disable shadows from overlapping on certain windows... I feel like I've done this before but I can't find any relevant options.

Try entering "any&!(class=dock)" in the CCSM > Window Decorations > options box for shadows.  It might also be type=dock, or instead of dock use panel, I can't remember.  Let me know if you have trouble finding the place to enter it!  It'll remove shadows from all your panels.

### Post by sertse on 2009-09-14
links2 using Facebook. links2 -g using Facebook, It should also be possible in Elinks, but I haven't worked out where to change the user agent on that yet.

It's actually "functional" as well. You can still post wall items and status changes, search your friends etc.  It's limitations aside from graphics are not much worse than if you're using on a regular browser with javascript off or noscript on.

### Post by yabbadabbadont on 2009-09-14
> **perfectska04 said:**
> Minor update from last night. Managed to make it a bit more netbook-friendly, without having to switch to a more compact theme.

Window list grouping + Workspaces takes care of the limited space in the top bar for open applications.

You can get a pretty slim (screenwise) setup using openbox.  I'm using it with your Shiki-Brave GTK+, gnome-brave icons, and Arc-Brave wallpaper.  Match them up with envyouraudience's Shiki/Dark Colors openbox themes, a properly configured tint2, and you have nice setup that doesn't take up too much screen space.  :D

[[img]http://omploader.org/tMmN0ZQ[/img]](http://omploader.org/vMmN0ZQ)  [[img]http://omploader.org/tMmN0Zg[/img]](http://omploader.org/vMmN0Zg)

Edit: Not that you can tell that from my 1280x1024 screenshots...  :lol:

### Post by perfectska04 on 2009-09-14
> **gymophett said:**
> I love this!
What fonts are those? Much loving.
&& if you don't mind, may I have your full font settings?
Such as px size and for each selection?

My fonts are the default "Sans" at size 8, it looks much better than Ubuntu's default font size. The window border font is set to "Bold". I did run the following command once, to get nicer fonts - but you shouldn't use it unless you know how to revert in case you dislike it:
```
sudo ln -sf /etc/fonts/conf.avail/10-autohint.conf /etc/fonts/conf.d/
```

> **yabbadabbadont said:**
> You can get a pretty slim (screenwise) setup using openbox.  I'm using it with your Shiki-Brave GTK+, gnome-brave icons, and Arc-Brave wallpaper.  Match them up with envyouraudience's Shiki/Dark Colors openbox themes, a properly configured tint2, and you have nice setup that doesn't take up too much screen space.  :D

I love crunchbang+openbox, but I'd only use them in my desktop PC. Whenever I try anything other than the main 3 DE's on a laptop/netbook, minor annoyances or missing functions ensue. For now I'm sticking with a stripped GNOME, unless it feels sluggish and I switch to XFCE or the new Netbook Remix.

### Post by perfectska04 on 2009-09-15
> **wersdaluv said:**
> perfectska04, just wanna ask... You make great GNOME and XFCE themes. What stops you from making themes for KDE 4 or using KDE 4? Don't you prefer its modern look? If Kubuntu was as polished as Ubuntu, would you choose Kubuntu with KDE 4 because of its look?

I prefer GNOME/XFCE because the overall desktop feels simpler and more intuitive. Besides, all the applications I use or care for are GTK-based, so switching to KDE doesn't really seem that enticing.

I do agree that Kubuntu is not as polished as other KDE distros, but the Karmic alphas are looking more functional and polished than ever.

---

### Post by wersdaluv on 2009-09-15
> **perfectska04 said:**
> I prefer GNOME/XFCE because the overall desktop feels simpler and more intuitive. Besides, all the applications I use or care for are GTK-based, so switching to KDE doesn't really seem that enticing.

I do agree that Kubuntu is not as polished as other KDE distros, but the Karmic alphas are looking more functional and polished than ever.
I'm dependent on gtk+ apps and the great "distro work" that Canonical does on its GNOME desktop that's why I can't make the switch. However, I am very much attracted by Qt 4's widget theme, Oxygen. I feel that it looks prettier and much more modern than gtk+.

Don't you think that Oxygen's look is superior to gtk+? Murrine is great but its glassy look feels very simple compared to Oxygen. Something like Aurora feels really modern but it's not as polished as Murrine or Clearlooks and it doesn't seem to be getting any further development. 

Just my two cents, though. I want to know what you think...

---

### Post by What is in a name? on 2009-09-15
> **wersdaluv said:**
> I'm dependent on gtk+ apps and the great "distro work" that Canonical does on its GNOME desktop that's why I can't make the switch. However, I am very much attracted by Qt 4's widget theme, Oxygen. I feel that it looks prettier and much more modern than gtk+.

Don't you think that Oxygen's look is superior to gtk+? Murrine is great but its glassy look feels very simple compared to Oxygen. Something like Aurora feels really modern but it's not as polished as Murrine or Clearlooks and it doesn't seem to be getting any further development. 

Just my two cents, though. I want to know what you think...

Honestly, the Murrine engine is one of the things I miss the most about Linux, now that I'm "having to" spend nearly all my time in Windows. Nowadays it's very versatile, and can have nearly any texture you wish, not only the traditional glassy one. I'd kill for some Murrine back in my life. *droolz*

*Sadface*.

### Post by What is in a name? on 2009-09-15

Those screenshots were taken on Windows. The visual style for XP was downloaded from here: [http://lassekongo83.deviantart.com/art/Capriccio-for-XP-137016994](http://lassekongo83.deviantart.com/art/Capriccio-for-XP-137016994). The GTK version is in this link: [http://lassekongo83.deviantart.com/art/Capriccio-GTK-137016638](http://lassekongo83.deviantart.com/art/Capriccio-GTK-137016638).

The wallpaper is DVNO, taken from [http://kon.deviantart.com/art/DVNO-116185112](http://kon.deviantart.com/art/DVNO-116185112).

I use IconPackager and the Arzo iconset: [http://yingjunjiu.deviantart.com/art/Arzo-Icons-81354404](http://yingjunjiu.deviantart.com/art/Arzo-Icons-81354404)

I use FindeXer for that left column in Explorer, with some assorted icons, and as for the toolbar, it's done with Styler. The folder of the theme is named 'MacStyle', but I can't find it anywhere on the Web at the moment. I can share it anyway, if necessary.

And the taskbar is just set to twice the regular size, because I usually have around 10-12 different apps open when I'm working on something, so I do need the room to see all the open tasks.

That said, Windows is a pain to customize. I miss Linux.

I used to create GTK themes when I used Linux, and I loved Murrine. However, I don't remember how it works, and meanwhile I bet new options were included by Andrea Cimitan, the developer. I just know it used to be my favourite engine, and still is, from what I can see on the themes that keep being released.

### Post by Sarai the Geek on 2009-09-16
> **Gorgoth said:**
> Any chance you could post your tint2 config? I've been trying to get the borders around my tint2 icon thingies and I just keep failing hard.
There's really not a whole lot of information out there about tint2 formatting. It's kind of trial and error...
```
#---------------------------------------------
# TINT2 CONFIG FILE
#---------------------------------------------
# For more information about tint2, see:
# http://code.google.com/p/tint2/wiki/Welcome
#
# For more config file examples, see:
# http://crunchbanglinux.org/forums/topic/3232/my-tint2-config/

#---------------------------------------------
# BACKGROUND AND BORDER
#---------------------------------------------

#background id 1--------------------------------------
rounded = 3
border_width = 2
background_color = #FFFFFF 50
border_color = #000000 60

#background id 2--------------------------------------
rounded = 3
border_width = 2
background_color = #FFFFFF 0
border_color = #000000 35

#background id 3--------------------------------------
rounded = 5
border_width = 0
#background_color = #A6B384 20
background_color = #ffffff 10
border_color = #000000 10

#background id 4--------------------------------------
rounded = 5
border_width = 0
#background_color = #A6B384 20
background_color = #ffffff 0
border_color = #000000 0

#---------------------------------------------
# PANEL
#---------------------------------------------
panel_monitor = all
#panel_mode = single_monitor
panel_position = bottom left
panel_size = 97% 28
panel_margin = 25 1
panel_padding = 3 3 3 3
font_shadow = 0
panel_background_id = 3


#---------------------------------------------
# TASKS
#---------------------------------------------
task_icon = 0
task_text = 1
task_width = 100
task_centered = 1
task_margin = 20
task_padding = 5
#task_icon_size = 13
task_font = Fontin Small Caps 10
task_font_color = #000000 35
task_active_font_color = #000000 100
task_background_id = 2
task_active_background_id = 1


#---------------------------------------------
# TASKBAR
#---------------------------------------------
taskbar_mode = single_monitor
taskbar_padding = 0 0 3
taskbar_background_id = 0

#---------------------------------------------
# SYSTRAYBAR
#---------------------------------------------
systray_padding = 0 0 0
systray_background_id = 1

#---------------------------------------------
# CLOCK
#---------------------------------------------
time1_format = %I:%M %P
time1_font = Fontin Small Caps 10
time1_font = Fontin Small Caps 10
#time2_format = %m.%e
#time2_font = Fontin Small Caps 10
clock_font_color = #000000 60
clock_padding = 4 0
clock_background_id = 1

#---------------------------------------------
# MOUSE ACTION ON TASK
#---------------------------------------------
mouse_middle = none
mouse_right = close
mouse_scroll_up = toggle
mouse_scroll_down = iconify
```

### Post by narf41 on 2009-09-17
> **etnlIcarus said:**
> How'd you get the borderless sidebar in nautilus?

it isn´t completely borderless, it has a width=1:


```
style "handle" = "default"
{

  GtkPaned::handle_size = 1
}

class "Gtk*Paned" style "handle"
```

---

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2009-09-17
> **narf41 said:**
> it isn´t completely borderless, it has a width=1:


```
style "handle" = "default"
{

  GtkPaned::handle_size = 1
}

class "Gtk*Paned" style "handle"
```

### Post by narf41 on 2009-09-17
from the howto in my biergarten2 package :) :
(the second mod is what you need)

modding the nautilus sidebar:

in terminal:
apt-get source nautilus
apt build-dep nautilus

1) changing iconsize for "places" view:

open ~/nautilus-(version)/src/nautilus-places-sidebar.c in (f.e.) gedit
search for "icon_size = nautilus_get_icon_size_for_stock_size (GTK_ICON_SIZE_MENU);"
change it to "icon_size = 24;" (or any other value)

2) deleting side-pane header:

make sure, your side-pane is set to "places-view"
open ~/nautilus-(version)/src/nautilus-side-pane.c
search for "gtk_box_pack_start (GTK_BOX (side_pane), frame, FALSE, FALSE, 0);"
change it to "//gtk_box_pack_start (GTK_BOX (side_pane), frame, FALSE, FALSE, 0);"

now, in terminal, go to ~/nautilus-(version)
./configure --prefix=/usr
make
sudo make install
killall nautilus




voila :)

---

### Post by Giant Speck on 2009-09-18
> **etnlIcarus said:**
> I'm not a fan of either. Aero is gaudy and Air has a lack of finish reminiscent of KDE3.x.

See, I love Air.  I think it is a very polished Plasma theme and is much better than any of the previous ones.

It's everything *else* about KDE 4 that I don't like.  I absolutely hate Bespin; I think it looks like crap.  I don't care how "customizable" it is, it still does not look very good to me.  

And if you don't want to use Bespin, than you either have to use a GTK theme (which almost defeats the purpose of using KDE) or one of the old styles like Oxygen, Plastic, and QtCurve.

The only KDE themes I have ever liked are Domino for KDE 3 and Skulpture for KDE 4, the latter of which is nice, but unlike the former, is not very customizable.

---

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2009-09-18
I appreciate that people have gone to the trouble of creating a clone-come-monster of blackbox, to make using Windows suck less but this is beyond a joke. Of the last 24 hours of my existence, I must've spent at least 8 of those trying to 'fix' bb4win_mod, so that it behaves sensibly. 5 of those hours would have gone into the menu alone, which seemed to have been configured by a team of sociopaths and sadists with poor communication skills.

Then, to add torture to torment, half way through Windows starts being a c***, forcing me to restart. And just as I think I'm finished; adding the bb4win_mod folder to my explorer sidebar, explorer decides to be a spaz and interprets the drag-and-drop (serves me right, but I don't know how else to add stuff to favourites on Windows) as a move gesture, rather than a, "create shortcut", one. It gets half way through moving all the files to god-knows-where (which shouldn't be possible anyway since this is a LIMITED ACCOUNT, as evidenced by the fact that Starsiege Tribes can't save any changes between sessions. Anyway, stuff turns up in Docs and settings\Icky\Favourites, go figure), before spitting the dummy because blackbox is running. At this point bb4win_mod was installed as my shell and half it's crucial files just went walky-byes. I figure out where the files have gone just in time for blackbox to lose it's **** and crash, breaking my shell. This is after I'd gone through the process of, "log out of main account, log into admin account, turn main account into an admin account, log back into main account and sent blackbox as shell, before going back to the admin account and un-doing the account changes", forcing me to go through it all again, albeit with a slightly modified agenda.

Anyway...

### Post by Gorgoth on 2009-09-18
-edit- Disregard this top bit... I solved it.

Menu borders: --> ~/.themes/[theme]/openbox-3/themerc
```

# Border colors
window.active.border.color: #fafafa
window.inactive.border.color: #fafafa
**menu.border.color: #000000**
window.active.client.color: #fafafa
window.inactive.client.color: #3E3C3A

```

Either way, desktop is still a WIP, and here's the current state:

Before:
[[IMG]http://img269.imageshack.us/img269/8514/wipq.th.png[/IMG]](http://img269.imageshack.us/i/wipq.png/)

After:
[[IMG]http://img9.imageshack.us/img9/6126/wip2m.th.png[/IMG]](http://img9.imageshack.us/i/wip2m.png/)

---

### Post by Sarai the Geek on 2009-09-20
> **Felliph3 said:**
> Ah thanks, any one else? Looks for me is 100% required so Im thinking that Gnome will be best but I want to try Openbox. I Gnome would be a bit snappier sometimes with Compiz, its not like it looks crazy amazing that it requires that much graphics. XFCE, Openbox, etc all look like minimalistic OSs and do I don't want to give up looks to have normal performance.

Go openbox or go home! Haha, I think openbox can look very good, but if you like lots of slick glossiness (you know what I'm talking about, right?) it may not be right for you. Personally, I can't stand all that garishness, I love the simplistic look of openbox, and I also like how configurable it is. It's also going to be quite a bit snappier than gnome, if by snappier you mean faster.
Basically, what I'm trying to get at is openbox is gorgeous, but it doesn't look great out of the box, you have to put some effort into it.
If you weren't around when I posted my last screenshot, it's here: [http://fc01.deviantart.com/fs50/f/2009/259/a/4/16_September_Screenshot_by_Sarai_the_Geek.png](http://fc01.deviantart.com/fs50/f/2009/259/a/4/16_September_Screenshot_by_Sarai_the_Geek.png). I'm using a pure openbox install (Crunchbang Lite) but you can use openbox in conjunction with gnome as a replacement for metacity.

### Post by londonali1010 on 2009-09-20
On the whole Crunchbang/Openbox topic...

I haven't done too much customisation yet, but so far the theming is better than Gnome, IMHO. That is, the themes seem to be more consistent within the theme (if that makes sense!). That said, I've given up my wobbly windows :( , shadows, transparency and my desktop cube (although you can get some of it back with xcompmgr and 3ddesktop), but I'm learning to dig the flat look.

Overall, I think the look is cleaner and less cluttered.

As far as Crunchbang goes, I went for Crunchbang Lite and it's perfect for me. The only programs I ever use are Skype, Rhythmbox, Chromium and GnuCash, so basically I just wanted them installed, and just the bare minimum to make the distro work...Crunchbang Lite is perfect for that because I can just download whatever I want from the Jaunty repos. Also, it took no tweaking, auto-detected all my weird netbook hardware, incl. wireless, so it was perfect. BTW, I tried it on a Live USB first, just to make sure :)

Oh, and I love just editing an XML file for all the menus, etc. Dead easy.

I've really noticed an improvement in performance (speed, not hanging, smoothness) as well over Gnome, although I have also upgraded my filesystem from ext2 to ext4, and I'm on a netbook, so Ubuntu/Gnome was always a bit heavy for me. Normal users might not notice a difference.

Oh, yeah, and it comes pre-loaded with Conky, so obviously I love it :KS

That's my 2p...I will have to do some tweaking and re-post with some Openbox eye candy :) Come on, Sarai, help me out here :)

---

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2009-09-20
Back on *nix. Was doing okay with XP, before it decided to spit the dummy at any app using Direct3D 9*, which led me to update my drivers, which led to me getting an error on startup and being unable to access CCC, which led to me spending several hours and several hundred MB of data in a vain attempt to fix it, which led me to uninstall CCC and install ATT in it's place, only to restart and *still* get the error message, which led to my going on a gun-toting rampage through the nearest computer store.

The irony is the only graphical problems I've had with this card on *nix were related to getting acceleration in WINE. XP has required 6 years of constant finicking and driver updates, and ATi *still* haven't managed to write a reliable driver for their own bloody card. I know WDM is a PITA to write drivers for but there is a limit to my patience.

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2009-09-20
> **sunchiqua said:**
> Would be great if you could share the details ( theme, icons, etc. ) - really nice setup :)

Okay, where to start...

Xfce4.6 + Compiz + Emerald.
wallpaper is from ladyrapid.deviantart.com
Emerald and GTK+ themes can be uploaded upon request - Gtk+ requires Murrine and Aurora engines.
Icon theme is Eikon2 (See What is in a name?'s sig).
Fonts are:
- Lucida Mac 8pt, 96DPI (Gtk+)
- Lucida Bold 8pt 96DPI (panel, window decorations).
- Segoe, bold, 7pt, 96DPI (RSS)
Slight hinting on all.

### Post by Islington on 2009-09-20
> **gymophett said:**
> Theme details pleasse?

GTK: dark ice, I did not like the glass menubar background so I changed it, but later decided to use Global Menu to save space.
Icons: Eikon, however the desktop folder icon is from a mod of mine.
Metacity: Chrono Dark Blue
Panel background: Chrono Dark Blue
Special gtkrc mods: turned off text shadows on desktop +changed text color; turned off the keyboard accelerators (the little underlines under words, that can be used with the alt button); turned panel text black.
wallpaper: found on /wg/ I can post it, if you want.

---

### Post by The Real Dave on 2009-09-20
> **londonali1010 said:**
> On the whole Crunchbang/Openbox topic...

I haven't done too much customisation yet, but so far the theming is better than Gnome, IMHO. That is, the themes seem to be more consistent within the theme (if that makes sense!). That said, I've given up my wobbly windows :( , shadows, transparency and my desktop cube (although you can get some of it back with xcompmgr and 3ddesktop), but I'm learning to dig the flat look.

Overall, I think the look is cleaner and less cluttered.

As far as Crunchbang goes, I went for Crunchbang Lite and it's perfect for me. The only programs I ever use are Skype, Rhythmbox, Chromium and GnuCash, so basically I just wanted them installed, and just the bare minimum to make the distro work...Crunchbang Lite is perfect for that because I can just download whatever I want from the Jaunty repos. Also, it took no tweaking, auto-detected all my weird netbook hardware, incl. wireless, so it was perfect. BTW, I tried it on a Live USB first, just to make sure :)

Oh, and I love just editing an XML file for all the menus, etc. Dead easy.

I've really noticed an improvement in performance (speed, not hanging, smoothness) as well over Gnome, although I have also upgraded my filesystem from ext2 to ext4, and I'm on a netbook, so Ubuntu/Gnome was always a bit heavy for me. Normal users might not notice a difference.

Oh, yeah, and it comes pre-loaded with Conky, so obviously I love it :KS

That's my 2p...I will have to do some tweaking and re-post with some Openbox eye candy :) Come on, Sarai, help me out here :)

I gotta agree, I had a 2.4Ghz Celeron, 512Mb RAM computer struggling with Jaunty and Gnome. I wanted to try out a few different WMs, so downloaded Openbox, Fluxbox and IceWM through Synaptic, but didn't want to spend time configuring them. Bought a Linux Format magazine, which included a Crunchbang Live CD, and I havn't looked back. Everything is alot faster and I love the minimalistic look. Plus, like the quote mentions, if you want any software, just get it from the repos, its still Ubuntu underneath :) perfect 

In regard to effects and that, this computer didn't have anywhere near enough power for Compiz, but is doing ok with compositioning in Crunchbang, though, I usually keep it off, its less strain on the CPU.

### Post by Sarai the Geek on 2009-09-20
> **londonali1010 said:**
> 
*snip!*
That's my 2p...I will have to do some tweaking and re-post with some Openbox eye candy :) Come on, Sarai, help me out here :)

Check out box-look.org or deviantart for openbox themes, play around with transparency in transset (part of xcompmgr- type "transset #" in a terminal where # is a decimal number between 0 and 1, press enter, then click on a window), read up on pipemenus and check out these scripts: [http://icculus.org/openbox/index.php/Openbox:Pipemenus](http://icculus.org/openbox/index.php/Openbox:Pipemenus).  :)

---

### Post by Tibuda on 2009-09-23
> **coldReactive said:**
> What if you absolutely hate fusion-icon? According to the how-to/manual there, you MUST have fusion-icon.

You don't need it. "compiz --replace ccp" does the job. I hate fusion-icon too. What a useless icon!

EDIT: I have read that thread again, and I have to agree: that howto is a mess (a mess that started me into compiz standalone). The important part is how to setup a custom session in GDM, creating a .desktop file in /usr/share/xsessions. The only required line in the compiz launcher is the "compiz ccp" line, but you'll get lost if you don't have a panel/launcher. You also need "nm-applet" to use a wireless network. Your Gtk+ applications will look like Windows 95 at first, so you have to tweak your ~/.gtkrc-2.0 file or use lxappearance or add gnome-settings-daemon to your launcher to import the gnome settings.

---

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2009-09-24
[url=http://img2.imageshack.us/img2/1955/screenshotca.jpg][img]http://img508.imageshack.us/img508/3568/screenshotsmall.jpg[/img]
http://img2.imageshack.us/img2/1955/screenshotca.jpg[/url]

Disabling tabs in Firefox and going old school ala multi-window.

Pros:
- Integration with desktop Scale/Expose.
- Can scrollwheel over tasklist to switch page.
- Switching pages is *a lot* more responsive.
- Get page thumbnails when moused-over tasklist.
- Extra screen real estate (pretty minor advantage, barely warrants mention).
- Improvement in overall usage consistency (rarely use tabs elsewhere).

Cons:
- Each open window causes about a 4-5mb jump in xserver memory usage. It's as bad as using Chrome.
- Composited environment means non-visible windows are still being repainted, which becomes burdensome even before you factor in animations. Only workaround is to manually minimise/shade each inactive window, to flush the pixmaps from cache (which ***** up Scale, plus they're planning to remove this behaviour from subsequent x.org releases, anyway).

Conclusion: I just wasted an hour of my life. However, the dream lives on...

Oh and for anyone who's interested (and has the hardware to pull it off):

middlemouse.openNewWindow = true
browser.tabs.opentabfor.middleclick = false
browser.tabs.autoHide = true
And in prefs, "When firefox starts: Show blank page".

---

### Post by &#32 Greg on 2009-09-24
> **PurposeOfReason said:**
> Giving xmonad a go with configs stolen from everywhere and modified to my tastes. Still trying to figure out if I can hide the current layout and window title, I don't care for either.
You probably have something that looks kind of like this...
```

 myPP :: Handle -> PP
            myPP din = defaultPP
                { ppCurrent = xmobarColor focusColor ""
                , ppVisible = xmobarColor lightTextColor ""
                , ppHiddenNoWindows = xmobarColor lightBackgroundColor ""
                , ppUrgent = xmobarColor "red" "black"
                , ppSep = " · "
                , ppWsSep = ""
                , ppTitle = xmobarColor lightTextColor "".
		(\y -> case y of
		    _ -> ""
                )
                , ppOutput = hPutStrLn din
                , ppLayout = xmobarColor "#ffffff" "" .
                (\x -> case x of
                                      _ -> ""
               )

                }


```

The quickest workaround for getting rid of the things is adding in the parentheses parts (and the periods!) in the parts of your myPP

Anyway, mine:

---

### Post by SomeGuyDude on 2009-09-24
Can I say, though, the fusion-icon IS useful. For example:

1) Switching WM on the fly. When I go out and take my laptop with me, I switch to OpenBox so I can save a few minutes of battery life. Additionally, it doesn't play nice with Blender and other 3D apps, so switching temporarily is nice.

2) Ever had Compiz randomly shut off all the window borders? With fusion-icon you right-click it and hit "reload window manager" and bam, everything's back.

Just to, y'know, point out that the thing isn't TOTALLY useless. :P

### Post by Tipped OuT on 2009-09-24
> **yabbadabbadont said:**
> Just one more month until Halloween, and your desktop is already ready for it.  :D

What GTK+ theme is that?

It's a simple fusion of Dark Room and "Dust.

How to make it?

1. Select the Dark Room theme in Appearance.
2. Click customize.
3. Click on the "window border" tab and select Dust.
4. Go to the colors section and make it look like mine:

[IMG]http://img410.imageshack.us/img410/4278/screenshotcustomizethem.png[/IMG]

All done, enjoy.

[http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Darkroom?content=95284](http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Darkroom?content=95284)

There you go.

I didn't have the human-theme package installed, which contains it.  Then it was a simple matter of copying the DarkRoom gtkrc file and changing the gtk_color_scheme line to use the colors from the index.theme file you gave me.

Thank you.

(Now I just have to start dinking with my userChrome.css so that firefox behaves itself...)

### Post by dbbolton on 2009-09-25
> **chucky chuckaluck said:**
> huh?

The Ubuntu developers shipped plasma with superglued elements by default. Mark Shuttleworth described a workaround in his blog. You simply need to get some solvent- glass solvent works really well- and squirt it all over your monitor (go ahead and quote that out of context). Then you can put the widgets wherever you want.

### Post by Tipped OuT on 2009-09-26
> **enskillz said:**
> That's very nice, how did you get the transparency?

GTK Murrine engine. Try it for yourself, apply the "Dark Room" theme in System< Preferences< Appearance. Then open up System< Administration< System Monitor, and you'll notice the window is transparent.

### Post by coldReactive on 2009-09-26
> **Felliph3 said:**
> How did you get rhythmbox to be seethrough?

Compiz can do that (TM)

on opacity, saturation, etc. under opacity tab

set type=Normal in the window specific settings and opacity to XX percent

---

### Post by Tipped OuT on 2009-09-26
> **Felliph3 said:**
> I really like transparency, however that doesn't do the same as it seems to be doing it for him, I dont want transparent windows, I want parts of the windows tranparent and the letters be at normal opacity.

By using compiz for that it makes the whole window x% opacity. 

I have no idea where to get the murrine engine or how to install it? I got a murrine theme but its not showing up like that :confused::confused:

Well, if you're running Ubuntu. Then you should have a theme called "Dark Room". This is a perfect example of a theme that uses the Murrine engine.

Set that as your theme, then go to *System< Administration< System Monitor*, and notice how the window is now transparent.

---

### Post by Tipped OuT on 2009-09-26
> **Felliph3 said:**
> Yeah I saw that darklooks has transparency but then again I sure as hell don't want a dark brown theme!

I need that murrine engine bad, I need Rhythmbox to be see-through like that, I hate to compile because Im not good at it but I'll try that I guess. 

Anyways, my current look, theres been a lot of changing and it just keep getting better!

My goal is to comapre a screenshot of Windows 7, Mac OS X, and Ubuntu. That way I can show that Linux can look just as good as the other 2 operating systems and be just as useful.

If you want transparency in Rhythmbox then just install this patch:

[http://www.cimitan.com/murrine/node/81](http://www.cimitan.com/murrine/node/81)

Download the latest version.

Extract it.

Open up nautilus, press CTRL+H (to show hidden files). Now move the extracted folder to /home/.gnome2/rhythmbox/plugins

Most likely you will have to create that directory. No big deal.

Now start up Rhythmbox, go to Edit< Plugins and activate the RGBA plugin. Restart Rhythmbox.

Done.

---

### Post by ad_267 on 2009-09-27
> **ajy0852 said:**
> I took both these screenshots with scrot, no different settings or anything. I wonder why one is 10x the size (KB) of the other.

Well one's a PNG and the other's a JPEG, but I'm guessing the forum software converted the one without any windows open to JPG because it was too large.

It's because of the lossless compression algorithm used by PNG, it's a lot better suited to things with flat colours and text like your open windows. PNG's compression works poorly with noisy images like your background, but JPEG's lossy compression is much better suited to this type of image.

More info: [http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Portable_Network_Graphics](http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Portable_Network_Graphics)

---

### Post by PacSci on 2009-09-27
My desktop, on a fresh laptop install of Xubuntu.

My wallpaper is, of course, the great Jedi Knight Obi-Wan Kenobi. (For a slightly less noticeable touch, I replaced the "Applications" icon with the Old Republic symbol.) I also added a fairly standard Conky and made my default font Liberation Sans.

Also, I color-coded my terminals. White on black is fish, green on black is bash, gold on blue is Python, white on blue is Lua, and white on gray is Haskell. The terminal icon in my panel is actually a menu that lets me open any of those.

### Post by enskillz on 2009-09-28
> **chucky chuckaluck said:**
> what apps are those? which themes?


The GTK and icons are Nimbus
[http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/nimbus+%28ubuntu+and+debian%29?content=54755]("http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/nimbus+%28ubuntu+and+debian%29?content=54755")

Apps are Terminal and VLC player.

VLC has the default theme (as I found some of the themes can be a bit buggy and heavy) but the default runs smooth.

The firefox is Shiretoko (firefox 3.5) and for me runs like a dream.

### Post by cbrinegar on 2009-09-30
Here's a screenshot of a gray theme with compiz, a gnome panel, and awn dock for my widescreen laptop.  The theme uses components from others and tweaks some colors (gnome-themes-extras is installed).  My main goal has been to come up with a panel/dock layout that is more convenient for me.  I've tried to come up with something that gives more vertical space for firefox (awn auto hides) and makes my most used tools easily available (on the transparent gnome panel).  The wallpaper I show is a built-in one for an example, since I normally rotate my own photos in and out.

[IMG]http://brinegar.homelinux.com/private/jaunty_laptop_sep_2009_thumb.jpg[/IMG]

[Here is the theme file.]("http://brinegar.homelinux.com/private/CBDark.tgz")
[Full sized screenshot]("http://brinegar.homelinux.com/private/jaunty_laptop_sep_2009.png")

### Post by Crunchy the Headcrab on 2009-09-30
> **cbrinegar said:**
>  I've tried to come up with something that gives more vertical space for firefox (awn auto hides) and makes my most used tools easily available (on the transparent gnome panel).

I've always wondered if there is a way to force AWN under other windows.  I don't like how autohide works, but I don't like it sitting on top of my applications.  Anyone know, if this is possible?

---

### Post by fela on 2009-09-30
> **Crunchy the Headcrab said:**
> I've always wondered if there is a way to force AWN under other windows.  I don't like how autohide works, but I don't like it sitting on top of my applications.  Anyone know, if this is possible?

With compiz you can do this, using the window rules plugin. Just use class=awn (or whatever it is, might be avant-window-navigator, you can use the grab function). Put whatever it is into the 'keep below' entry in window rules settings in ccsm.

---

### Post by Crunchy the Headcrab on 2009-09-30
Thanks.  I figured it was probably a compiz thing.  :)

---

### Post by fela on 2009-09-30
> **Crunchy the Headcrab said:**
> Thanks.  I figured it was probably a compiz thing.  :)

Not just compiz: I think kwin has this feature too, if you like to use AWN in KDE.
